<Name>Erica Daniel<//Name><Time>1565205879933</Time><Rating>4</Rating>< Text>
4 stars for the food, 3 stars for the ambience. It was Way too loud!!! In the end I had to shout and left with a sore throat after dinner. It was like been to a club. I don't understand why it was so loud inside, maybe a lot of the crazy kids nearby coming for celebration.

But food was good. We came during the DineLA time. It was great they had the 1.5 hour unlimited drinks. So we had a lot of sangria. We ordered several dishes to share.

The cheese plate, a big plate and many varieties of cheese and cured meat.

I really like the polenta with eggplant. Crispy polenta was very tasty and went great with the eggplant sauce. It was pretty full after 4 sticks.

The cauliflower, it was not that memorable. Didn't remember the taste.

The burger was pretty big, and tasty. Well, the runny egg makes everything better. I don't eat meat, so I will not be able to comment on burger any more.

The dessert was not that memorable either. Can't remember how it tasted.

Probably because it was too loud inside, the experience wasn't that great. But I like their menu, and lots of options for vegetarians.< /Text>

This place is mainly for finger foods and drinks. Tried the Chicken wings, Gorgonzola pasta, Bacaro fries, Grilled chicken breast and Mushroom pizza.
All of them were tasty but my favourites were the wings and the fries. The fries come with a fried egg on top and when mixed, the flavour is amazing.

They have 90 Min bottomless drinks for 20$ per person. You can order either red/ White wine, Sangria, Prosecco or Beer. You can also switch between drinks which is a great option. The vibe of the place is divey and the service is great too. (Thanks Ron!)< /review>

<name>JR C<//name>< text>
Eats: Bacaro Burger with Fried Egg, Roasted Garlic Grilled Pizza, Oven Roasted Bone Marrow, Bacaro Mac and Cheese with Bacon.

I was lucky enough to grab the last table on a Monday night. If that's how it is on Mondays, I see this place easily filled on other nights. The Roasted Garlic Grilled Pizza was the clear winner here. There was a good spice in the sauce which surprised us. A second bite got a bit more spicier, which wasn't bad at all. Good flavor in a flatbread pizza. The Bacaro Burger with Fried Egg was second best. This open faced burger got most of it's flavor from the seasoned medium rare beef. Even the fried egg on top wasn't too necessary, if only to make the open face burger prettier to look at. I'm a typical burger fan so this isn't really a surprise.

The bone marrow and the mac and cheese were a bit of a letdown. The bone marrow was served with 4 pieces of bruschetta bread which to me did not match any of our other tapas dishes in terms of flavor or quantity. It was neat to try once, but I'd probably just grab another burger instead as I would have enjoyed that more. The mac and cheese was not as flavorful as it could have been either even with the truffle help. There's more menu items to choose from which also looked plenty enticing, so just another reason to return.< /text>

<user_id>110411655962160480227<//user_id>< name>
Parker G<//name>
< time>
1490168256816</time>
<Rate>2<//Rate>< text>
I was very unimpressed with Bacaro.  I feel like the only reason it does well is because it's one of the few trendy restaurants in proximity of USC.  The food here is certainly good, but the tapa-sized portions are very overpriced and rather underwhelming.

First off, I did not enjoy the cramped, small, dark space inside.  It's probably part of the vibe or atmosphere that they try to create for their restaurant, but it wasn't cutting it for me.  You can barely see inside of the dimly lit interior at night, and the benches for seats are weird and uncomfortable.  Everything feels very tight.

The food itself is very good.  I enjoyed the fries and the macaroni.  They have a lot of simple casual food items such as this.  Do NOT get the Bacaro burger and expect an actual hamburger.  It was the most disappointing and sad looking slab of meat on a piece of bread that I have ever seen.  IT'S NOT A BURGER IF IT DOESN'T HAVE TWO BUNS!!!  Disappointing.

Not worth the cost.  Only plus is the convenience of its location close to USC.  I'll look elsewhere further away, however, for much better dining experiences that are worth the cost.< /text>

<Response>None</Response>< review>
This place is pretty neat. I've been a bunch of times so when Living Social had a $40 for $20 deal many months ago, I grabbed it... and then waited until the last possible day to use it. There were three of us. We each chose two dishes (six total) and I think that was just enough to leave us pleasantly full, but not overstuffed.

We had:
baguette with olive oil (not part of our 6 items)
cauliflower with chipotle aioli and mixed greens
pan-seared scallops
artichoke hearts
and three things from the specials menu written on the chalkboard (sorry, I can't remember what they were)

I had a glass of a white blend and a glass of Tintero Moscato (which was, as always, deliciously sweet).

One of the really neat things about this place is that the owners and staff are not pretentious at all about wine. Can't pronounce the name of the wine you want? Who cares? Butcher it. Want to try something before you commit to a glass or a bottle? Go for it! Not sure what to get but know (at least, generally) what you like? Tell your server and have him recommend something.

It's a small place, so be prepared to wait if it's busy. If you're not in a rush, I'd say stick it out (even if the line is long).< /review>

<Name>Pauline Cao</Name>< Review>
I went here for Happy Hour (Monday - Thursday 5PM-7PM) with my girls on a Wednesday night and was not disappointed. All the portions are tapas size so order away!

What We Ordered:
- Poached Shrimp
- Burrata Di Gioia
- Bacon and Brie Pizza
- Glazed Pork Belly Skewers****
- Crispy Pig Ears
- Lamb Stuffed Eggplant****
- Oven Roasted Bone Marrow
- Mac & Cheese****
- Grilled Hangar Steak****
- Sangria

Everything was so good!! My favorite items are ****.... We ordered 5 orders of the Glazed Pork Belly Skewers!! It was melt in your mouth good. I don't think anyone else really liked the Lamb Stuffed Eggplant...but I really did! It was not gamey and had a lot of good flavor! The Mac & Cheese was perfectly cooked and had the right amount of cheesiness! Most restaurants don't add enough cheese so it's just noodles and bland sauce. This was definitely not the case! The Grilled Hangar Steak was very tender and cooked to a perfect medium rare. All the other items we ordered were good as well!

I do not recommend the Bacon and Brie Pizza. It was just average. The Sangria tasted like juice but, it hit us all later hahah.. granted we had 3 pitchers among 5 girls. :) If it wasn't so far, I would come here more often! They also had an all you can drink sangria option. I will have to try that out next time!</Review>

<Review>Been meaning to try Bacaro for awhile now since I've heard good things so I was really excited to see them on Groupon! I picked up a deal for AYCD and 8 tapas for 4 people and had a great experience. I was worried that it wouldn't be enough food since everything is in small portions for sharing, but I think the AYCD filled us up so the amount of food was perfect.

Bacaro has about 30-40 different tapas to choose from, including cold and hot dishes, mini pizzas, and dessert. If you're thinking these tapas only make up the appetizer portion of their menu, think again. That's all they have! We had no idea which tapas to choose so we picked randomly and had our server recommend a few to us as well. The memorable ones were the bacaro burger, the hangar steak, the fries, and the mac and cheese. I would pass on the Tal's Tower since it's mainly just bread and the shrimp included were pathetically small. I would also pass on the pork belly skewers since it was too sweet and fatty for my taste. I mean I know it's pork belly, but some pieces were seriously all fat.

The groupon made this meal extremely worth it since normally AYCD is $20/person and each tapas is $8 (or 3 for $21). Btw, the AYCD includes only their Bacaro beer, champagne, sangria, and wine for 90 minutes. If you're worried you won't get the most out of your AYCD because you have to wait for your server, I recommend sitting at the bar. That's what we did and our server was on top of it!

If you have a party of 6 or more, be sure to make reservations. This place gets packed since it's right by USC. Parking can be a pain since it's only street. Overall, I had a great time at Bacaro and would return, but I would probably try to go for happy hour when everything is a bit cheaper.<//Review><Pics>None</Pics><Response>None</Response><gmapID>0x80c2c7ec5d711435:0xc4e5b8e93183c6c9<//gmapID></record></dataset><record>

< user_name>
Karen Wang< /user_name>
<Text>Definitely one of my favorite tapas spots in LA. I really connected with this cool hole in the wall and the happy hour menu that came with.

M-TH 5-7PM: 5$ tapas and housemade Sangria specials!

FOOD to share:
* Cauliflower with Chipotle Aioli: smoky, spicy, slightly tangy...take note, this will make you like your veggies / cauliflower!

* Fried Egg Pizza: thin, potentially flaky crisp crust, super soft, barely set egg on cheese and something green.

* Poached Shrimp with lots of basil and Sweet Chili Sauce: good shrimp swimming in lots of sweeter-than-spicy (or tangy) chili sauce; slightly reminiscent of something Asian, and the basil...win!

* Eggplant stuffed Lamb with Lemon Garlic Emulsion: such a memorable concoction! there's a slice of fried lemon that totally adds to the cheese-topped eggplant lamb. The lemon and garlic emulsion is the perfect component to this. Enough said.

* Dessert: Panini with Bicycle Honey Wheat Bread, Nutella and Banana: sweet sandwich grilled? yes. not too sweet and the best part, they use bicycle bread! love that co.

AMBIENCE
This place is dressed in all dark features: floor to ceiling chalkboard walls plastered with big writing listing out different wines, beers and other beverages.

A key interior feature is of course the wine bottle ceiling. You'll also quickly notice the other creative wine bottle lighting and furnishings around. There are lots of small wooden panel tables for two that can be pieced together like a puzzle, which means this place has the flexibility for larger parties (also larger table seating in the adjacent area).

Seats are pretty comfy but if you sit along the central small tables and long booth area, you'll be cozy close to your neighbors...in which case, makes for the proper time and place to stare and point, ooo and ahh about what other people are ordering.

PARKING
Street out front or around the corner/neighborhood.</Text></record></dataset><record>

<review>I'm an RC Rock Crawler/Trail/monster truck rig guy for over 33 years.
Marty's hasn't been there 33+ years but they have a huge selection of crawler rigs that are ready-to-run(RTR). They have a huge selection of replacement parts , from Axial to Traxxas including aftermarket parts like SSD, RC4WD and Pro-line(among others), soft lexan and hardbodies. The staff are hobbiest so they are knowledgeable on what they have.....or I wouldn't drive nearly two hours to get there.
You could easily spend several hours playing on their indoor trail/rock course.
They have fast stuff for carpet racing, bashing and trains and flying stuff. I'm not into that so I can't tell you how extensive that part is.
But if you love trail/rock rigs and monster trucks like I do...this is an awesome place. If they don't have it , they will get it.<//review>< username>

Marty's Hobbies new location has more space, even enough to accommodate several indoor race courses! <Date>1499344970797<//Date>< rate>
3<//rate>
< text>
Decent selection relative to the size of shop.  Good selection of parts for R/C planes, helis, multi-rotors, cars / trucks and also model supply including trains.  Downside is, just like every small business local hobby shop now, it is completely unrealistic to consider buying anything here unless you need it the same day or sooner.  Prices are up to ten times that of the comparable online retailer, even with shipping or next day delivery.  You would only be buying something here in an emergency or if you just don't know any better.  That being said, it is nice that there is still a hobby shop of this type anywhere around, this is one of the last left within fifty miles.  Staff is moderately friendly.</text>

<user>101580676906619213372< /user>< Review>
I had a very pleasant experience. The food was very exceptional. Having spent some time in Italy myself (and having to eat out for every meal), I confidently found that the authenticity was unquestionable and very delicious. Another comment here mentioned octopus, which I had as an appetizer. If there was something I had to recommend in particular from my meal, this would surely be it.

I was also very pleased by the service. This was personally the second time I've been here ‚Äî first time being when I was probably in diapers when it just opened...so I was pretty much a new customer again. It was evident that there are returning customers, yet my table was given the same friendly and dedicated service as everyone else. We had constant communication and acknowledgement from the waiter and passing staff. The food tasted and was prepared in an upscale fashion, but the service was family-esque. Very complete restaurant, plan to go back.< /Review>

Incredibly underwhelmed with this experience. I ordered take out over the phone and was quoted 20 minutes. I got there on time, was greeted after standing for a couple minutes. They asked me what name the order was under but I hadn't been asked for a name. The server disappeared for a moment, walked back out and didn't say anything to me. After another 5 minutes, a woman came out, said it would be a moment and then left. Another 10 minutes later and I finally got rung up, and the food was out in another 5. Total of 20 minutes of waiting. The woman I placed the order with most certainly forgot to put it in to the kitchen and didn't just explain the mistake and apologize. It was not busy enough for a 40 minute wait time to feel justified. There was little communication about my order and it overall felt pretentious and like I was not worth their time. The food was mediocre at best, I ordered the Ravioli and at the price of $21, I feel like I could have made better at home. The side of bread I was given was stale. Who the hell serves stale bread? According to the other reviews, the bread usually comes with a pesto dipping sauce for it. Never got any. I should have just taken the drive and gone to Spiazzo Ristorante in West Portal. Won't be coming back here again.<//Text>

Came here for lunch and was promptly seated outside.  After that, service was good to a bit slow, as has been noted in other reviews.  As I write this, I've been waiting about 5 minutes for them to take my check.  Come on guys, I want to give you money and free up a table.

<Pics>None<//Pics><review>HRMM. I was curious about Flores since they opened on Sawtelle, a decidedly non-Japanese eatery and with such a curious name! Finally made it here on a Friday night around 8:45pm. We were seated right away on the patio.

FOOD:
We were so looking forward to the soft shell crab sandwich but they no longer had it on the menu! Sadness.
- baked hen egg - this was pretty good! Kinda like a hash, but no potatoes, there were thick chunks of ham in it as well.
- sausage stuffed quail - SALTY. The quail was very easy to cut in half, and chock full of sausage, which made it all salty! The stuffing underneath kinda absorbed some oil from the chicken - I didn't eat it.
- papardelle with braised rabbit - this was my favorite dish. The papardelle noodles were SO GOOD! So wide and thick, cooked perfectly and not too saucy. The rabbit itself was super lean and kinda chewy.

SERVICE:
SLOW. I think we sat for about 10 minutes before we were greeted by our server. The guy who brought us our food was friendly and nice, I liked him but our server wasn't very friendly, didn't introduce himself and was hard to flag down.

VENUE/PARKING:
Place is cute, with indoor and outdoor patio seating. Their heat lamps work amazingly well! Bathrooms are single stall per gender, and are VERY dim. Street parking wasn't too hard to find. I think they have valet for $7.< /review><gmap_id>0x80c2bb74e4bd4295:0x13a7954fa61f6520</gmap_id>< rate>

<Rating>3</Rating>< text>
Once one of my favorite markets, the renovation a few years back seems to have diminished Gelson's appeal. Surely that's not what renovations are made to do, and there are some positive outcomes including the improved cheese section and more space in several areas. Something about the new color/lighting makes it feel like you've been transported to a medical clinic in the 1970's. The prices, as ever, are terribly high. There used to be some competition as to whether Gelson's or Whole Foods would more quickly drain my bank account, but Gelson's has very clearly pulled ahead. Gelson's also seems to have a habit of banishing some of my favorite products (some that I could only find at Gelson's) from its shelves...likely due to a matter of the store's limited footprint, but annoying nevertheless. Considering they have less of what I want, and are charging horrendous prices for stuff I can easily find elsewhere, my visits here have become fewer and far between. One bright spot: They still have the best deli department anywhere, with wonderful and friendly staff behind the counter. My favorite irrepressible redhead knows who she is, but they're all a pleasure, and, in fact, earn Gelson's an extra star on their own.</text>

< review>
BECAUSE PRICES ARE MUCH HIGHER ON NEARLY EVERY ITEM THAN ANY OTHER MARKET.. I AM GIVING 4 STARS..OTHERWISE 5 STARS IT WOULD BE. OK...This IS my neighborhood market now and has been for many years. This market is impeccably clean, well stocked, superbly managed and customer service is superior! The prices do reflect the quality of merchandise..you will NOT see empty spaces on these shelves for more than 3 mins.! Like produce..yes. It is expensive but I have NEVER tasted a sweeter ear of corn or better bigger Bing cherries. This market caters to an area that houses the likes of very high profile celebrities.. TV personalities, actors from box office blockbusters (say that fast 3 times!) to local news anchors. THEY HAVE MONEY TO BUY THE BEST..AND IT'S HERE!! If you want to do your weekly shopping here, you should be able to spend up to 9 bucks for a PINT of the best ice cream and $16-25 (free range) for an average size chicken . I'm not wealthy AT ALL..but I do treat myself on the excellent sushi, deli and baked goods pretty regularly!  Prepare for POSSIBLE parking issues between 5 and 7 pm. THERE IS AMPLE PARKING..95% of the time.  Otherwise..Albertsons is not too far away.  Some staff have been at Gelsons (was Mayfair) for at least 20-25 years. Most I've known 17+ years .. still very friendly! Photos coming soon.. Right here!</review>
